					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Dr. Dre</span></h1>
							
<div id="p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown mw-portlet mw-portlet-lang"  >
	<input type="checkbox" id="p-lang-btn-checkbox" role="button" aria-haspopup="true" data-event-name="ui.dropdown-p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown-checkbox mw-interlanguage-selector" aria-label="Go to an article in another language. Available in 76 languages"   >
	<label id="p-lang-btn-label" for="p-lang-btn-checkbox" class="vector-dropdown-label cdx-button cdx-button--fake-button cdx-button--fake-button--enabled cdx-button--weight-quiet cdx-button--action-progressive mw-portlet-lang-heading-76" aria-hidden="true"  ><span class="vector-icon mw-ui-icon-language-progressive mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-language-progressive"></span>

<span class="vector-dropdown-label-text">76 languages</span>
	</label>
	<div class="vector-dropdown-content">

		<div class="vector-menu-content">
			
			<ul class="vector-menu-content-list">

					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American rapper and record producer (born 1965)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Doctor Dre" and "Andre Young" redirect here. For the rapper and MTV VJ, see <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Dr%C3%A9" title="Doctor Dré">Doctor Dré</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Andre_Young_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Andre Young (disambiguation)">Andre Young (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Andre Romell  Young</b> (born February 18, 1965), known professionally as <b>Dr. Dre</b>, is an American rapper and record producer. He is the founder and <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beats_Electronics" title="Beats Electronics">Beats Electronics</a>, and previously co-founded, co-owned, and was the president of <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a>. Dr. Dre began his career as a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Class_Wreckin%27_Cru" title="World Class Wreckin&#39; Cru">World Class Wreckin' Cru</a> in 1985 and later found fame with the <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> group <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>. The group popularized explicit lyrics in <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> to detail the violence of street life. During the early 1990s, Dre was credited as a key figure in the crafting and popularization of <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast</a> <a href="/wiki/G-funk" title="G-funk">G-funk</a>, a subgenre of hip hop characterized by a <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizer</a> foundation and slow, heavy beats.
</p><p>Dre's solo debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic" title="The Chronic">The Chronic</a></i> (1992), released under Death Row Records, made him one of the best-selling American music artists of 1993. It earned him a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance">Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance</a> for the single "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Ride" title="Let Me Ride">Let Me Ride</a>", as well as several accolades for the single "<a href="/wiki/Nuthin%27_but_a_%27G%27_Thang" title="Nuthin&#39; but a &#39;G&#39; Thang">Nuthin' but a 'G' Thang</a>". That year, he produced Death Row labelmate <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Doggy Dogg</a>'s debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Doggystyle" title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a></i> and mentored producers such as his stepbrother <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a> (leading to the multi-platinum debut <i><a href="/wiki/Regulate...G_Funk_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulate...G Funk Era">Regulate...G Funk Era</a></i> in 1994) and Snoop Dogg's cousin <a href="/wiki/Daz_Dillinger" title="Daz Dillinger">Daz Dillinger</a> (leading to the double-platinum debut <i><a href="/wiki/Dogg_Food" title="Dogg Food">Dogg Food</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound" title="Tha Dogg Pound">Tha Dogg Pound</a> in 1995), as well as mentor to upcoming producers <a href="/wiki/Sam_Sneed" title="Sam Sneed">Sam Sneed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melvin_%22Mel-Man%22_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Melvin &quot;Mel-Man&quot; Bradford">Mel-Man</a>. In 1996, Dr. Dre left Death Row Records to establish his own label, Aftermath Entertainment. He produced a compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre_Presents_the_Aftermath" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr. Dre Presents the Aftermath">Dr. Dre Presents the Aftermath</a></i>, in 1996, and released a solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/2001_(Dr._Dre_album)" title="2001 (Dr. Dre album)">2001</a></i>, in 1999.
</p><p>During the 2000s, Dre focused on producing other artists, occasionally contributing vocals. He signed <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> in 1998 and <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> in 2002, and co-produced their albums. He has produced albums for and overseen the careers of many other rappers, including <a href="/wiki/The_D.O.C." title="The D.O.C.">the D.O.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xzibit" title="Xzibit">Xzibit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knoc-turn%27al" title="Knoc-turn&#39;al">Knoc-turn'al</a>, <a href="/wiki/Game_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Game (rapper)">the Game</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anderson_.Paak" title="Anderson .Paak">Anderson .Paak</a>. Dre has also had acting roles in movies such as <i><a href="/wiki/Set_It_Off_(film)" title="Set It Off (film)">Set It Off</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wash_(2001_film)" title="The Wash (2001 film)">The Wash</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Training_Day" title="Training Day">Training Day</a></i>. He has won seven <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Producer_of_the_Year,_Non-Classical" title="Grammy Award for Producer of the Year, Non-Classical">Producer of the Year, Non-Classical</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked him number 56 on the list of <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_Greatest_Artists_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone&#39;s 100 Greatest Artists of All Time">100 Greatest Artists of All Time</a>. He was the second-richest figure in hip hop as of 2018 with an estimated net worth of $800 million.
</p><p>Accusations of Dre's violence against women have been widely publicized. Following his assault of television host <a href="/wiki/Dee_Barnes" title="Dee Barnes">Dee Barnes</a>, he was fined $2,500, given two years' probation, ordered to perform 240 hours of <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a>, and given a spot on an anti-violence <a href="/wiki/Public_service_announcement" title="Public service announcement">public service announcement</a>. A civil suit was settled out of court. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Michel%27le" title="Michel&#39;le">Michel'le</a>, the mother of one of his children, accused him of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> during their time together as a couple. Their abusive relationship is portrayed in her 2016 biopic <i><a href="/wiki/Surviving_Compton:_Dre,_Suge_%26_Michel%27le" title="Surviving Compton: Dre, Suge &amp; Michel&#39;le">Surviving Compton: Dre, Suge &amp; Michel'le</a></i>. Lisa Johnson, the mother of three of Dr. Dre's children, stated that he beat her many times, including while she was pregnant. She was granted a restraining order against him. Former labelmate <a href="/wiki/Tairrie_B" title="Tairrie B">Tairrie B</a> claimed that Dre assaulted her at a party in 1990, in response to her track "Ruthless Bitch". Two weeks following the release of his third album, <a href="/wiki/Compton_(album)" title="Compton (album)"><i>Compton</i></a> in August 2015, he issued an apology to the women "I've hurt".<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Andre Romell Young<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo20071_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo20071-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> was born in <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a>, on February 18, 1965,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> the son of Theodore and Verna Young. His middle name is derived from the Romells, his father's amateur <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> group. His parents married in 1964, separated in 1968, and divorced in 1972. His mother later remarried to Curtis Crayon and had three children: sons Jerome and Tyree (both deceased) and daughter Shameka.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo20076–8,_25_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo20076–8,_25-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1976, Dre began attending Vanguard Junior High School in Compton, but due to <a href="/wiki/Gang_violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Gang violence">gang violence</a>, he transferred to the safer suburban Roosevelt Junior High School.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo20079_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo20079-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The family moved often and lived in apartments and houses in Compton, <a href="/wiki/Carson,_California" title="Carson, California">Carson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California" title="Long Beach, California">Long Beach</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Watts,_Los_Angeles" title="Watts, Los Angeles">Watts</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Los_Angeles" title="South Los Angeles">South Central</a> neighborhoods of Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Dre has said that he was mostly raised by his grandmother in the New Wilmington Arms housing project in Compton.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His mother later married Warren Griffin,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo200710_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo200710-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> which added three step-sisters and one step-brother to the family; the latter would eventually begin rapping under the name <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKenyatta200114_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKenyatta200114-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Dre is also the cousin of producer <a href="/wiki/Sir_Jinx" title="Sir Jinx">Sir Jinx</a>.
Dre attended <a href="/wiki/Centennial_High_School_(Compton,_California)" title="Centennial High School (Compton, California)">Centennial High School</a> in Compton during his freshman year in 1979, but transferred to <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fremont_High_School" title="John C. Fremont High School">Fremont High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Los_Angeles" class="mw-redirect" title="South Central Los Angeles">South Central Los Angeles</a> due to poor grades. He attempted to enroll in an apprenticeship program at <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Corporation" title="Northrop Corporation">Northrop Aviation Company</a>, but poor grades at school made him ineligible. Thereafter, he focused on his social life and entertainment for the remainder of his high school years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo20072_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo20072-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dre's frequent absences from school jeopardized his position as a diver on his school's swim team. After high school, he attended Chester Adult School in Compton following his mother's demands for him to get a job or continue his education. After brief attendance at a radio broadcasting school, he relocated to the residence of his father and residence of his grandparents before returning to his mother's house.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo200718–19_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo200718–19-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1985.E2.80.931986:_World_Class_Wreckin.27_Cru"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1985–1986:_World_Class_Wreckin'_Cru">1985–1986: World Class Wreckin' Cru</span></h3>
<p>Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Grandmaster_Flash" title="Grandmaster Flash">Grandmaster Flash</a> song "<a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Grandmaster_Flash_on_the_Wheels_of_Steel" title="The Adventures of Grandmaster Flash on the Wheels of Steel">The Adventures of Grandmaster Flash on the Wheels of Steel</a>", Dr. Dre often attended a club called Eve's After Dark to watch many DJs and rappers performing live. He subsequently became a DJ in the club, initially under the name "Dr. J", based on the nickname of <a href="/wiki/Julius_Erving" title="Julius Erving">Julius Erving</a>, his favorite basketball player. At the club, he met aspiring rapper Antoine Carraby, later to become member <a href="/wiki/DJ_Yella" title="DJ Yella">DJ Yella</a> of <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKenyatta200115_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKenyatta200115-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Soon afterwards he adopted the moniker Dr.&#160;Dre, a mix of previous alias Dr. J and his first name, referring to himself as the "Master of Mixology".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo200714_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo200714-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Eve After Dark had a back room with a small four-track studio. In this studio, Dre and Yella recorded several demos. In their first recording session, they recorded a song entitled "Surgery".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo200723_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo200723-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Dr. Dre's earliest recordings were released in 1994 on a compilation titled <i><a href="/wiki/Concrete_Roots" title="Concrete Roots">Concrete Roots</a></i>. Critic <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of <a href="/wiki/Allmusic" class="mw-redirect" title="Allmusic">allmusic</a> described the compiled music, released "several years before Dre developed a distinctive style", as "surprisingly generic and unengaging" and "for dedicated fans only".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dre later joined the musical group <a href="/wiki/World_Class_Wreckin%27_Cru" title="World Class Wreckin&#39; Cru">World Class Wreckin' Cru</a>, which released its debut album under the Kru-Cut label in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo200726_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo200726-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The group would become stars of the electro-hop scene that dominated early-mid 1980s <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast hip hop</a>. "Surgery", which was officially released after being recorded prior to the group's official formation, would prominently feature Dr.&#160;Dre on the turntable. The record would become the group's first hit, selling 50,000&#160;copies within the Compton area.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKenyatta200114–15_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKenyatta200114–15-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Dr.&#160;Dre and DJ Yella also performed mixes for local radio station <a href="/wiki/KBLA" title="KBLA">KDAY</a>, boosting ratings for its afternoon rush-hour show <i>The Traffic Jam</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERo200717_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERo200717-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1986.E2.80.931991:_N.W.A_and_Ruthless_Records"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1986–1991:_N.W.A_and_Ruthless_Records">1986–1991: N.W.A and Ruthless Records</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-left listen noprint listen-left"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style>
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:N.W.A_-_Fuck_Tha_Police.ogg" title="File:N.W.A - Fuck Tha Police.ogg">"Fuck Tha Police"</a></div>
<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="30" data-mwtitle="N.W.A_-_Fuck_Tha_Police.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9b/N.W.A_-_Fuck_Tha_Police.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (69 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/9/9b/N.W.A_-_Fuck_Tha_Police.ogg/N.W.A_-_Fuck_Tha_Police.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><track src="/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AN.W.A_-_Fuck_Tha_Police.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬" data-dir="ltr" /></audio></span></span></div>
<div class="description">from <i><a href="/wiki/Straight_Outta_Compton" title="Straight Outta Compton">Straight Outta Compton</a></i></div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg/170px-Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="214" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg/255px-Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg/340px-Uncle_Jam%27s_Army_-_Eazy-E_and_N.W.A._1988_Skateland_Concert_Poster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="813" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption>Poster for one of N.W.A's first concerts at a Compton skating rink, 1988</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1986, Dr. Dre met rapper O'Shea Jackson—known as <a href="/wiki/Ice_Cube" title="Ice Cube">Ice Cube</a>—who collaborated with him to record songs for <a href="/wiki/Ruthless_Records" title="Ruthless Records">Ruthless Records</a>, a hip hop record label run by local rapper <a href="/wiki/Eazy-E" title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a>. <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a> and fellow West Coast rapper <a href="/wiki/Ice-T" title="Ice-T">Ice-T</a> are widely credited as seminal artists of the gangsta rap genre, a profanity-heavy subgenre of hip hop, replete with gritty depictions of urban crime and gang lifestyle. Not feeling constricted to racially charged political issues pioneered by rap artists such as <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Enemy (band)">Public Enemy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Boogie_Down_Productions" title="Boogie Down Productions">Boogie Down Productions</a>, N.W.A favored themes and uncompromising lyrics, offering stark descriptions of violent, inner-city streets. Propelled by the hit "<a href="/wiki/Fuck_tha_Police" title="Fuck tha Police">Fuck tha Police</a>", the group's first full album <i><a href="/wiki/Straight_Outta_Compton" title="Straight Outta Compton">Straight Outta Compton</a></i> became a major success, despite an almost complete absence of radio airplay or major concert tours. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> sent Ruthless Records a warning letter in response to the song's content.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Ice Cube left N.W.A in 1989 over financial disputes, Dr. Dre produced and performed for much of the group's second album <i><a href="/wiki/Efil4zaggin" class="mw-redirect" title="Efil4zaggin">Efil4zaggin</a></i>. He also produced tracks for a number of other acts on Ruthless Records, including Eazy-E's 1988 solo debut <i><a href="/wiki/Eazy-Duz-It" title="Eazy-Duz-It">Eazy-Duz-It</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Above_the_Law_(group)" title="Above the Law (group)">Above the Law</a>'s 1990 debut <i><a href="/wiki/Livin%27_Like_Hustlers" title="Livin&#39; Like Hustlers">Livin' Like Hustlers</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Michel%27le" title="Michel&#39;le">Michel'le</a>'s 1989 <a href="/wiki/Michel%27le_(album)" title="Michel&#39;le (album)">self-titled debut</a>, the D.O.C.'s 1989 debut <i><a href="/wiki/No_One_Can_Do_It_Better" title="No One Can Do It Better">No One Can Do It Better</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/J.J._Fad" class="mw-redirect" title="J.J. Fad">J.J. Fad</a>'s 1988 debut <i><a href="/wiki/Supersonic_(J._J._Fad_album)" title="Supersonic (J. J. Fad album)">Supersonic</a></i> and funk rock musician <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Z" class="mw-redirect" title="Jimmy Z">Jimmy Z</a>'s 1991 album <i><a href="/wiki/Muzical_Madness" title="Muzical Madness">Muzical Madness</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-doc_formula_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doc_formula-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1991.E2.80.931996:_The_Chronic_and_Death_Row_Records"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1991–1996:_The_Chronic_and_Death_Row_Records">1991–1996: <i>The Chronic</i> and Death Row Records</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1134653256"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096940132"><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr._Dre_-_Nuthin%27_But_a_%22G%22_Thang.ogg" title="File:Dr. Dre - Nuthin&#39; But a &quot;G&quot; Thang.ogg">"Nuthin' But a 'G' Thang"</a></div>
<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="30" data-mwtitle="Dr._Dre_-_Nuthin&#39;_But_a_&quot;G&quot;_Thang.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fe/Dr._Dre_-_Nuthin%27_But_a_%22G%22_Thang.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (60 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/f/fe/Dr._Dre_-_Nuthin%27_But_a_%22G%22_Thang.ogg/Dr._Dre_-_Nuthin%27_But_a_%22G%22_Thang.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><track src="/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3ADr._Dre_-_Nuthin%27_But_a_%22G%22_Thang.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬" data-dir="ltr" /></audio></span></span></div>
<div class="description">from <i>The Chronic</i></div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>After a dispute with Eazy-E, Dre left the group at the peak of its popularity in 1991 under the advice of friend, and N.W.A lyricist, the D.O.C. and his bodyguard at the time, <a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight" title="Suge Knight">Suge Knight</a>. Knight, a notorious strongman and intimidator, was able to have Eazy-E release Young from his contract and, using Dr.&#160;Dre as his flagship artist, founded <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a>. In 1992, Young released his first single, the <a href="/wiki/Deep_Cover_(song)" title="Deep Cover (song)">title track</a> to the film <i><a href="/wiki/Deep_Cover" title="Deep Cover">Deep Cover</a></i>, a collaboration with rapper <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, whom he met through Warren G.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Dr.&#160;Dre's debut solo album was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic" title="The Chronic">The Chronic</a></i>, released under Death Row Records with Suge Knight as executive producer. Young ushered in a new style of rap, both in terms of musical style and lyrical content, including introducing a number of artists to the industry including Snoop Dogg, <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daz_Dillinger" title="Daz Dillinger">Daz Dillinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/RBX" title="RBX">RBX</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Lady_of_Rage" title="The Lady of Rage">the Lady of Rage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jewell_(singer)" title="Jewell (singer)">Jewell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr._Dre_logo_b.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Dr._Dre_logo_b.png/220px-Dr._Dre_logo_b.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="35" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Dr._Dre_logo_b.png/330px-Dr._Dre_logo_b.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Dr._Dre_logo_b.png/440px-Dr._Dre_logo_b.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="96" /></a><figcaption>Logo used by <i>Chronic</i>-era Dr. Dre</figcaption></figure>
<p>On the strength of singles such as "<a href="/wiki/Nuthin%27_but_a_%22G%22_Thang" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuthin&#39; but a &quot;G&quot; Thang">Nuthin' but a 'G' Thang</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Ride" title="Let Me Ride">Let Me Ride</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Fuck_wit_Dre_Day_(and_Everybody%27s_Celebratin%27)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuck wit Dre Day (and Everybody&#39;s Celebratin&#39;)">Fuck wit Dre Day (and Everybody's Celebratin')</a>" (known as "Dre Day" for radio and television play), all of which featured Snoop Dogg as guest vocalist, <i>The Chronic</i> became a cultural phenomenon, its <a href="/wiki/G-funk" title="G-funk">G-funk</a> sound dominating much of hip hop music for the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) certified the album triple platinum,<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and Dr.&#160;Dre also won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance">Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance</a> for his performance on "Let Me Ride".<sup id="cite_ref-grammy_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> For that year, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine also ranked Dr.&#160;Dre as the eighth best-selling musical artist, <i>The Chronic</i> as the sixth best-selling album, and "Nuthin' but a 'G' Thang" as the 11th best-selling single.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_life_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop_life-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:California_Love_(1995),_by_Tupac_Shakur.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/California_Love_%281995%29%2C_by_Tupac_Shakur.png/220px-California_Love_%281995%29%2C_by_Tupac_Shakur.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/California_Love_%281995%29%2C_by_Tupac_Shakur.png 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="262" /></a><figcaption>"California Love" earned Dr. Dre his first number one spot on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and two <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> nominations.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Besides working on his own material, Dr.&#160;Dre produced Snoop Dogg's debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Doggystyle" title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a></i>, which became the first debut album for an artist to enter the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> album charts at number one.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In 1994 Dr.&#160;Dre produced some songs on the soundtracks to the films <i><a href="/wiki/Above_the_Rim" title="Above the Rim">Above the Rim</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Was_the_Case" title="Murder Was the Case">Murder Was the Case</a></i>. He collaborated with fellow N.W.A member Ice Cube for the song "<a href="/wiki/Natural_Born_Killaz" title="Natural Born Killaz">Natural Born Killaz</a>" in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> For the film <i><a href="/wiki/Friday_(1995_film)" title="Friday (1995 film)">Friday</a></i>, Dre recorded "<a href="/wiki/Keep_Their_Heads_Ringin%27" title="Keep Their Heads Ringin&#39;">Keep Their Heads Ringin'</a>", which reached number ten on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and number 1 on the Hot Rap Singles (now Hot Rap Tracks) charts.<sup id="cite_ref-dr-dre-sin_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dr-dre-sin-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1995, Death Row Records signed rapper <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">2Pac</a>, and began to position him as their major star: he collaborated with Dr. Dre on the commercially successful single "<a href="/wiki/California_Love" title="California Love">California Love</a>", which became both artists' first song to top the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> However, in March 1996 Young left the label amidst a contract dispute and growing concerns that label boss Suge Knight was corrupt, financially dishonest and out of control. Later that year, he formed his own label, Aftermath Entertainment, under the distribution label for Death Row Records, <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, Death Row Records suffered poor sales by 1997, especially following the death of 2Pac and the <a href="/wiki/Racket_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Racket (crime)">racketeering</a> charges brought against Knight.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dr. Dre also appeared on the single "<a href="/wiki/No_Diggity" title="No Diggity">No Diggity</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> group <a href="/wiki/Blackstreet" title="Blackstreet">Blackstreet</a> in 1996: it too was a sales success, topping the Hot 100 for four consecutive weeks, and later won the award for Best R&amp;B Vocal by a Duo or Group at the <a href="/wiki/1997_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="1997 Grammy Awards">1997 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> After hearing it for the first time, several of Dr. Dre's former Death Row colleagues, including 2Pac, recorded and attempted to release a song titled "<a href="/wiki/Toss_It_Up" title="Toss It Up">Toss It Up</a>", containing numerous insults aimed at Dr. Dre and using a deliberately similar instrumental to "No Diggity", but were forced to replace the production after Blackstreet issued the label with a <a href="/wiki/Cease_and_desist" title="Cease and desist">cease and desist</a> order stopping them from distributing the song.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.932000:_Move_to_Aftermath_Entertainment_and_2001"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–2000:_Move_to_Aftermath_Entertainment_and_2001">1996–2000: Move to Aftermath Entertainment and <i>2001</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png/220px-Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="38" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png/330px-Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png/440px-Dr_Dre_2001_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="93" /></a><figcaption>Logo used by <i>2001</i>-era Dr. Dre</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre_Presents_the_Aftermath" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr. Dre Presents the Aftermath">Dr. Dre Presents the Aftermath</a></i> album, released on November 26, 1996, featured songs by Dr.&#160;Dre himself, as well as by newly signed <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> artists, and a solo track "<a href="/wiki/Been_There,_Done_That_(Dr._Dre_song)" title="Been There, Done That (Dr. Dre song)">Been There, Done That</a>", intended as a symbolic farewell to <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Despite being classified platinum by the RIAA,<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> the album was not very popular among music fans.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In October 1996, Dre performed "Been There, Done That" on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, Dr. Dre produced several tracks on <a href="/wiki/The_Firm_(hip_hop_group)" title="The Firm (hip hop group)">the Firm</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Album_(The_Firm_album)" title="The Album (The Firm album)">The Album</a></i>; it was met with largely negative reviews from critics. Rumors began to abound that Aftermath was facing financial difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Aftermath Entertainment also faced a <a href="/wiki/Trademark_infringement" title="Trademark infringement">trademark infringement</a> lawsuit by the underground thrash metal band Aftermath.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/First_Round_Knock_Out" title="First Round Knock Out">First Round Knock Out</a></i>, a compilation of various tracks produced and performed by Dr. Dre, was also released in 1996, with material ranging from World Class Wreckin' Cru to N.W.A to Death Row recordings.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Dr. Dre chose to take no part in the ongoing <a href="/wiki/East_Coast%E2%80%93West_Coast_hip_hop_rivalry" title="East Coast–West Coast hip hop rivalry">East Coast–West Coast hip hop rivalry</a> of the time, instead producing for, and appearing on, several New York artists' releases, such as <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>' "Nas Is Coming", <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Zoom_(Dr._Dre_song)" title="Zoom (Dr. Dre song)">Zoom</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s "Watch Me".
</p><p>The turning point for Aftermath came in 1998, when Dre's close friend, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>, the co-founder of Interscope Records (parent label for Aftermath), suggested that Dr. Dre sign <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, a white rapper from <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>. Dre produced three songs and provided vocals for two on Eminem's successful and controversial debut album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Slim_Shady_LP" title="The Slim Shady LP">The Slim Shady LP</a></i>, released in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-em-bio_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-em-bio-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The Dr. Dre-produced lead single from that album, "<a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is" title="My Name Is">My Name Is</a>", brought Eminem to public attention for the first time, and the success of <i>The Slim Shady LP</i> – it reached number two on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and received general acclaim from critics – revived the label's commercial ambitions and viability.<sup id="cite_ref-em-bio_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-em-bio-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1134653256"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096940132"><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">

<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_2" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="29" data-mwtitle="Dr._Dre_-_Still_D.R.E..ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/94/Dr._Dre_-_Still_D.R.E..ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (68 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/9/94/Dr._Dre_-_Still_D.R.E..ogg/Dr._Dre_-_Still_D.R.E..ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><track src="/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3ADr._Dre_-_Still_D.R.E..ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬" data-dir="ltr" /></audio></span></span></div>

<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg/220px-Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="84" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg/330px-Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg/440px-Up_in_Smoke_Tour_concert_ticket_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1113" data-file-height="427" /></a><figcaption>Ticket for Dr. Dre's <a href="/wiki/Up_in_Smoke_Tour" title="Up in Smoke Tour">Up in Smoke Tour</a> in Albany, New York, July 2000</figcaption></figure>
<p>Dr.&#160;Dre's second solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/2001_(Dr._Dre_album)" title="2001 (Dr. Dre album)">2001</a></i>, released on November 16, 1999, was considered an ostentatious return to his gangsta rap roots.<sup id="cite_ref-2001_amg_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_amg-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It was initially titled <i>The Chronic 2000</i> to imply being a sequel to his debut solo effort <i>The Chronic</i> but was re-titled <i>2001</i> after Death Row Records released an unrelated compilation album with the title <i><a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight_Represents:_Chronic_2000" title="Suge Knight Represents: Chronic 2000">Suge Knight Represents: Chronic 2000</a></i> in May 1999. Other tentative titles included <i>The Chronic 2001</i> and <i>Dr.&#160;Dre</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-changes_2001_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-changes_2001-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album featured numerous collaborators, including <a href="/wiki/Devin_the_Dude" title="Devin the Dude">Devin the Dude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xzibit" title="Xzibit">Xzibit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knoc-turn%27al" title="Knoc-turn&#39;al">Knoc-turn'al</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_T" title="King T">King T</a>, Defari, <a href="/wiki/Kokane" title="Kokane">Kokane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> and new protégé <a href="/wiki/Hittman_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hittman (rapper)">Hittman</a>, as well as co-production between Dre and new Aftermath producer <a href="/wiki/Melvin_%22Mel-Man%22_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Melvin &quot;Mel-Man&quot; Bradford">Mel-Man</a>. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of the website <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> described the sound of the album as "adding ominous <a href="/wiki/Strings_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Strings (music)">strings</a>, soulful vocals, and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>" to Dr.&#160;Dre's style.<sup id="cite_ref-2001_amg_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_amg-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The album was highly successful, charting at number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> charts<sup id="cite_ref-drecharts_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drecharts-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and has since been certified six times platinum,<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> validating a recurring theme on the album: Dr.&#160;Dre was still a force to be reckoned with, despite the lack of major releases in the previous few years. The album included popular hit singles "<a href="/wiki/Still_D.R.E." title="Still D.R.E.">Still D.R.E.</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Forgot_About_Dre" title="Forgot About Dre">Forgot About Dre</a>", both of which Dr.&#160;Dre performed on NBC's <i>Saturday Night Live</i> on October 23, 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Dr.&#160;Dre won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Producer_of_the_Year,_Non-Classical" class="mw-redirect" title="Producer of the Year, Non-Classical">Producer of the Year, Non-Classical</a> in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and joined the <a href="/wiki/Up_in_Smoke_Tour" title="Up in Smoke Tour">Up in Smoke Tour</a> with fellow rappers Eminem, Snoop Dogg, and Ice Cube that year as well.<sup id="cite_ref-up_in_smoke_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-up_in_smoke-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932010:_Focus_on_production_and_Detox"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000–2010:_Focus_on_production_and_Detox">2000–2010: Focus on production and <i>Detox</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr._Dre.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dr._Dre.jpg/170px-Dr._Dre.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="252" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dr._Dre.jpg/255px-Dr._Dre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dr._Dre.jpg/340px-Dr._Dre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="594" /></a><figcaption>Dr. Dre in 2008</figcaption></figure>
<p>Following the success of <i>2001</i>, Dr.&#160;Dre focused on producing songs and albums for other artists. He co-produced six tracks on Eminem's landmark <i><a href="/wiki/Marshall_Mathers_LP" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall Mathers LP">Marshall Mathers LP</a></i>, including the Grammy-winning lead single, "<a href="/wiki/The_Real_Slim_Shady" title="The Real Slim Shady">The Real Slim Shady</a>". The album itself earned a Grammy and proved to be the fastest-selling rap album of all time, moving 1.76&#160;million units in its first week alone.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He produced the single "<a href="/wiki/Family_Affair_(Mary_J._Blige_song)" title="Family Affair (Mary J. Blige song)">Family Affair</a>" by R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> for her album <i><a href="/wiki/No_More_Drama" title="No More Drama">No More Drama</a></i> in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-wealth_2001_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wealth_2001-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He also produced "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Blow_Ya_Mind" title="Let Me Blow Ya Mind">Let Me Blow Ya Mind</a>", a duet by rapper <a href="/wiki/Eve_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eve (entertainer)">Eve</a> and <a href="/wiki/No_Doubt" title="No Doubt">No Doubt</a> lead singer <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and signed R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Truth_Hurts_(singer)" title="Truth Hurts (singer)">Truth Hurts</a> to Aftermath in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dr. Dre produced and rapped on singer and Interscope labelmate <a href="/wiki/Bilal_(American_singer)" title="Bilal (American singer)">Bilal</a>'s 2001 single "<a href="/wiki/Fast_Lane_(Bilal_song)" title="Fast Lane (Bilal song)">Fast Lane</a>", which barely missed the <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">Top 40</a> of the R&amp;B charts.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> He later assisted in the production of Bilal's second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Love_for_Sale_(Bilal_album)" title="Love for Sale (Bilal album)">Love for Sale</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> which Interscope controversially shelved because of its creative direction.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Dr. Dre was the executive producer of Eminem's 2002 release, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Eminem_Show" title="The Eminem Show">The Eminem Show</a></i>. He produced three songs on the album, one of which was released as a <a href="/wiki/Business_(song)" title="Business (song)">single</a>, and he appeared in the award-winning video for "<a href="/wiki/Without_Me_(Eminem_song)" title="Without Me (Eminem song)">Without Me</a>". He also produced the D.O.C.'s 2003 album <i><a href="/wiki/Deuce_(The_D.O.C._album)" title="Deuce (The D.O.C. album)">Deuce</a></i>, where he made a guest appearance on the tracks "Psychic Pymp Hotline", "Gorilla Pympin'" and "Judgment Day".
</p><p>In 2002, Dr. Dre signed rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> to Aftermath in a joint venture between Interscope and Eminem's Shady Records. Dr. Dre served as executive producer for 50 Cent's commercially successful February 2003 debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin%27_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Get Rich or Die Tryin&#39; (album)">Get Rich or Die Tryin'</a></i>. Dr. Dre produced or co-produced four tracks on the album, including the hit single "<a href="/wiki/In_da_Club" title="In da Club">In da Club</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Eminem's fourth album since joining Aftermath, <i><a href="/wiki/Encore_(Eminem_album)" title="Encore (Eminem album)">Encore</a></i>, again saw Dre taking on the role of executive producer, and this time he was more actively involved in the music, producing or co-producing a total of eight tracks, including three singles.
</p><p>Dr.&#160;Dre also produced "<a href="/wiki/How_We_Do_(song)" title="How We Do (song)">How We Do</a>", a 2005 hit single from rapper <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">the Game</a> from his album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Documentary" title="The Documentary">The Documentary</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-kingmaker_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingmaker-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> as well as tracks on 50 Cent's successful second album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Massacre" title="The Massacre">The Massacre</a></i>. For an issue of <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine in April 2005, Dr. Dre was ranked 54th out of 100 artists for <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine's list "The Immortals: The Greatest Artists of All Time". <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> wrote the summary for Dr. Dre, where he stated Dr. Dre's song "Xxplosive" as where he "got (his) whole sound from".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2006, Dr.&#160;Dre began working with <a href="/wiki/Raekwon" title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a> on his album <i><a href="/wiki/Only_Built_4_Cuban_Linx_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Only Built 4 Cuban Linx II">Only Built 4 Cuban Linx II</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> He also produced tracks for the rap albums <i><a href="/wiki/Buck_the_World" title="Buck the World">Buck the World</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Curtis_(50_Cent_album)" title="Curtis (50 Cent album)">Curtis</a></i> by 50 Cent,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Blue_Carpet_Treatment" title="Tha Blue Carpet Treatment">Tha Blue Carpet Treatment</a></i> by Snoop Dogg,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Come_(Jay-Z_album)" title="Kingdom Come (Jay-Z album)">Kingdom Come</a></i> by Jay-Z.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Dre also appeared on <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>'s track "Bounce", from his 2007 solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Timbaland_Presents_Shock_Value" class="mw-redirect" title="Timbaland Presents Shock Value">Timbaland Presents Shock Value</a></i> alongside, <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> During this period, the D.O.C. stated that Dre had been working with him on his fourth album <i>Voices through Hot Vessels</i>, which he planned to release after <i>Detox</i> arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Planned but unreleased albums during Dr.&#160;Dre's tenure at Aftermath have included a full-length reunion with Snoop Dogg titled <i>Breakup to Makeup</i>, an album with fellow former N.W.A member Ice Cube which was to be titled <i>Heltah Skeltah</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-doc_formula_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doc_formula-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> an N.W.A reunion album,<sup id="cite_ref-doc_formula_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doc_formula-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and a joint album with fellow producer <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> titled <i>Chairmen of the Board</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-no_nwa_reunion_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-no_nwa_reunion-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Dr. Dre's third studio album, formerly known as <i>Detox</i>, was slated to be his final studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_2007_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_2007-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Work for the upcoming album dates back to 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-Dr._Dre&#39;s_Final_Album_Will_Be_Hip-Hop_Musical_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dr._Dre&#39;s_Final_Album_Will_Be_Hip-Hop_Musical-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> where its first version was called "the most advanced rap album ever", by producer <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dr._Dre&#39;s_Detox_&#39;The_Most_Advanced_Rap_Album_Ever,&#39;_Co-Producer_Says_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dr._Dre&#39;s_Detox_&#39;The_Most_Advanced_Rap_Album_Ever,&#39;_Co-Producer_Says-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Later that same year, he decided to stop working on the album to focus on producing for other artists, but then changed his mind; the album had initially been set for a fall 2005 release.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Producers confirmed to work on the album include <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khalil" title="DJ Khalil">DJ Khalil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottz" title="Nottz">Nottz</a>, Bernard "Focus" Edwards Jr.,<sup id="cite_ref-focus_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-focus-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hi-Tek" title="Hi-Tek">Hi-Tek</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J.R._Rotem" class="mw-redirect" title="J.R. Rotem">J.R. Rotem</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/RZA" title="RZA">RZA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> claimed that <i>Detox</i> was finished, according to a June 2008 report by <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After another delay based on producing other artists' work, <i>Detox</i> was then scheduled for a 2010 release, coming after 50 Cent's <i><a href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct" title="Before I Self Destruct">Before I Self Destruct</a></i> and Eminem's <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)" title="Relapse (Eminem album)">Relapse</a></i>, an album for which Dr. Dre handled the bulk of production duties.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/Dr_Pepper" title="Dr Pepper">Dr Pepper</a> commercial that debuted on May 28, 2009, he premiered the first official snippet of <i>Detox</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Dr_Pepper_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Dr_Pepper-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dr_Pepper_ad_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dr_Pepper_ad-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> 50 Cent and Eminem asserted in a 2009 interview on <a href="/wiki/BET" title="BET">BET</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park</a></i> that Dr. Dre had around a dozen songs finished for <i>Detox</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 15, 2008, Dre appeared in the remix of the song "<a href="/wiki/Set_It_Off_(Kardinal_Offishall_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Set It Off (Kardinal Offishall song)">Set It Off</a>" by Canadian rapper <a href="/wiki/Kardinal_Offishall" title="Kardinal Offishall">Kardinal Offishall</a> (also with <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Pusha T</a>); the remix debuted on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Skee" title="DJ Skee">DJ Skee</a>'s radio show.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of 2009, Dre produced, and made a guest vocal performance on, the single "<a href="/wiki/Crack_a_Bottle" title="Crack a Bottle">Crack a Bottle</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> and the single sold a record 418,000 downloads in its first week<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> and reached the top of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart on the week of February 12, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Along with this single, in 2009 Dr. Dre produced or co-produced 19 of 20 tracks on Eminem's album <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)" title="Relapse (Eminem album)">Relapse</a></i>. These included other hit singles "<a href="/wiki/We_Made_You" title="We Made You">We Made You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Old_Time%27s_Sake" title="Old Time&#39;s Sake">Old Time's Sake</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/3_a.m._(Eminem_song)" title="3 a.m. (Eminem song)">3 a.m.</a>" (The only track Dre did not produce was the Eminem-produced single "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Eminem_song)" title="Beautiful (Eminem song)">Beautiful</a>".).
</p><p>On April 20, 2010, "Under Pressure", featuring <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and co-produced with <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a>, was confirmed by Jimmy Iovine and Dr. Dre during an interview at <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a> as the album's first single.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The song leaked prior to its intended release in an unmixed, unmastered form without a chorus on June 16, 2010;<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> however, critical reaction to the song was lukewarm, and Dr. Dre later announced in an interview that the song, along with any other previously leaked tracks from <i>Detox</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s recording process, would not appear on the final version of the album.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two genuine singles – "<a href="/wiki/Kush_(song)" title="Kush (song)">Kush</a>", a collaboration with Snoop Dogg and fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/I_Need_a_Doctor" title="I Need a Doctor">I Need a Doctor</a>" with Eminem and singer <a href="/wiki/Skylar_Grey" title="Skylar Grey">Skylar Grey</a> – were released in the United States during November 2010 and February 2011 respectively:<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> the latter achieved international chart success, reaching number four on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and later being certified double platinum by the RIAA and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA).<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On June 25, 2010, the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers</a> honored Dr. Dre with its Founders Award for inspiring other musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932020:_The_Planets.2C_hiatus.2C_Coachella.2C_and_Compton"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2020:_The_Planets,_hiatus,_Coachella,_and_Compton">2010–2020: <i>The Planets</i>, hiatus, Coachella, and <i>Compton</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg/220px-Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg/330px-Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg/440px-Dr._Dre_at_Coachella_2012_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="562" data-file-height="683" /></a><figcaption>Dr. Dre performs at the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival#2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">2012 Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In an August 2010 interview, Dr. Dre stated that an <a href="/wiki/Instrumental" title="Instrumental">instrumental</a> album, <i>The Planets</i>, was in its first stages of production; each song being named after a <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> On September 3, Dr. Dre showed support to longtime protégé <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, and appeared on his and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Home_%26_Home_Tour" title="The Home &amp; Home Tour">Home &amp; Home Tour</a>, performing hit songs such as "Still D.R.E.", "Nuthin' but a 'G' Thang", and "Crack a Bottle", alongside Eminem and another protégé, 50 Cent. Sporting an "R.I.P. Proof" shirt, Dre was honored by Eminem telling Detroit's <a href="/wiki/Comerica_Park" title="Comerica Park">Comerica Park</a> to do the same. They did so, by chanting "DEEE-TOX", to which he replied, "I'm coming!"<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 14, 2011, Dre announced that he would be taking a break from music after he finished producing for artists <a href="/wiki/Slim_the_Mobster" title="Slim the Mobster">Slim the Mobster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>. In this break, he stated that he would "work on bringing his Beats By Dre to a standard as high as Apple" and would also spend time with his family.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On January 9, 2012, Dre headlined the final nights of the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a> in April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2014, <a href="/wiki/Marsha_Ambrosius" title="Marsha Ambrosius">Marsha Ambrosius</a> stated that she had been working on Detox, but added that the album would be known under another title .<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In September 2014, Aftermath in-house producer <a href="/wiki/Dawaun_Parker" title="Dawaun Parker">Dawaun Parker</a> confirmed the title change and stated that over 300 beats had been created for the album over the years, but few of them have had vocals recorded over them.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The length of time that <i>Detox</i> had been recorded for, as well as the limited amount of material that had been officially released or leaked from the recording sessions, had given it considerable notoriety within the music industry.<sup id="cite_ref-dj-quik-detox_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dj-quik-detox-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Numerous release dates (including the ones mentioned above) had been given for the album over the years since it was first announced, although none of them transpired to be genuine.<sup id="cite_ref-hhwireddetox_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hhwireddetox-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-complex-detox_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-detox-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Several musicians closely affiliated with Dr. Dre, including Snoop Dogg, fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">the Game</a> and producer <a href="/wiki/DJ_Quik" title="DJ Quik">DJ Quik</a>, had speculated in interviews that the album will never be released, due to Dr. Dre's business and entrepreneurial ventures having interfered with recording work, as well as causing him to lose motivation to record new material.<sup id="cite_ref-hhwireddetox_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hhwireddetox-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-complex-detox_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-detox-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 1, 2015, Dre announced that he would release what would be his final album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Compton_(album)" title="Compton (album)">Compton</a></i>. It is inspired by the <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a> biopic, <i><a href="/wiki/Straight_Outta_Compton_(film)" title="Straight Outta Compton (film)">Straight Outta Compton</a></i>, and is a compilation-style album, featuring a number of frequent collaborators, including Eminem, Snoop Dogg, Kendrick Lamar, Xzibit and the Game, among others. It was initially released on <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a> on August 7, with a retail version releasing on August 21.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, he revealed that he had about 20 to 40 tracks for <i>Detox</i> but he did not release it because it did not meet his standards. Dre also revealed that he suffers from <a href="/wiki/Social_anxiety" title="Social anxiety">social anxiety</a> and due to this, remains secluded and out of attention.<sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 12, 2016, it was revealed that Apple would create its first original scripted television series for its then-upcoming <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV%2B" title="Apple TV+">Apple TV+</a> streaming service.<sup id="cite_ref-Dr._Dre_set_to_star_in_new_series_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dr._Dre_set_to_star_in_new_series-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Titled <i>Vital Signs</i>, it was set to reflect Dre's life.<sup id="cite_ref-Dr._Dre_set_to_star_in_new_series_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dr._Dre_set_to_star_in_new_series-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> He was also  an executive producer on the show<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> before the show's cancellation sometime in September 2018, due to an overly graphic concept of drugs, gun violence and sex.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In October 2016, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean Combs</a> brought out Dr. Dre, Snoop Dogg and others on his Bad Boy reunion tour.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, he produced four songs on <a href="/wiki/Oxnard_(album)" title="Oxnard (album)"><i>Oxnard</i></a> by <a href="/wiki/Anderson_.Paak" title="Anderson .Paak">Anderson .Paak</a>. He was the executive producer on the album, as so its follow-up, 2019's <i><a href="/wiki/Ventura_(Anderson_.Paak_album)" title="Ventura (Anderson .Paak album)">Ventura</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2020.E2.80.93present:_Return_to_production_and_Super_Bowl_halftime_show"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–present:_Return_to_production_and_Super_Bowl_halftime_show">2020–present: Return to production and Super Bowl halftime show</span></h3>
<p>Dr. Dre was the executive producer of Eminem's 2020 release, <i><a href="/wiki/Music_to_Be_Murdered_By" title="Music to Be Murdered By">Music To Be Murdered By</a></i>. He produced four songs on the album. He also produced two songs on the deluxe edition of the album, <i><a href="/wiki/Music_to_Be_Murdered_By#Music_to_Be_Murdered_By_–_Side_B_(Deluxe_Edition)" title="Music to Be Murdered By">Side B</a></i>, and appeared on the song, "Gunz Blazing". On September 30, 2021, it was revealed that Dre would perform at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LVI halftime show">Super Bowl LVI halftime show</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>. 
In December 2021, an update for the video game, <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_Online" title="Grand Theft Auto Online">Grand Theft Auto Online</a></i>, predominantly featured Dre and added some of his previously unreleased tracks which was released as an EP, <i>The Contract</i>, on February 3, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Around this time, Dre announced he was collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Marsha_Ambrosius" title="Marsha Ambrosius">Marsha Ambrosius</a> on <i>Casablanco</i>, and with Mary J. Blige on an upcoming album.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, Snoop Dogg announced that he and Dr. Dre are in the process of recording their new album, <i>Missionary</i>. Snoop said the album will be released via Death Row and Aftermath.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On February 13, 2022, Dr. Dre performed at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LVI halftime show">Super Bowl LVI halftime show</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> with surprise appearances from <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anderson._Paak" class="mw-redirect" title="Anderson. Paak">Anderson. Paak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The performance was met with critical acclaim and is the first Super Bowl halftime show to win the <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Variety_Special_(Live)" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Variety Special (Live)">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Variety Special (Live)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The show also won the Primetime Emmy Awards for <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Production_Design_for_a_Variety_Special" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Production Design for a Variety Special">Outstanding Production Design for a Variety Special</a> and <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Music_Direction" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Music Direction">Outstanding Music Direction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The same year, he produced numerous songs including "The King and I", a collaboration between Eminem and <a href="/wiki/CeeLo_Green" title="CeeLo Green">CeeLo Green</a> for the 2022 biopic, <i><a href="/wiki/Elvis_(2022_film)" title="Elvis (2022 film)">Elvis</a>,</i> and a remix of <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Use_This_Gospel" title="Use This Gospel">Use This Gospel</a>" for <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/God_Did" title="God Did">God Did</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In September 2022, it was reported that Dr. Dre will compose the original score for the upcoming animated series, <i>Death for Hire: The Origin of Tehk City</i>. The show is created by <a href="/wiki/Ice-T" title="Ice-T">Ice-T</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Prince" title="Arabian Prince">Arabian Prince</a>; based on the graphic novel of the same title, it features the voice talent of Ice-T, his wife Coco Austin, Snoop Dogg, <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Treach" title="Treach">Treach</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2023, Dre and Marsha Ambrosius held a listening party for the <i>Casablanco</i> album in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_appearances">Film appearances</span></h3>
